In his book, <i>The Illusion of Conscious Will,</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-201">[201]</a></sup> Wegner summarizes what he believes is <a href="/wiki/Empirical_evidence" title="Empirical evidence">empirical evidence</a> supporting the view that human perception of conscious control is an illusion. Wegner summarizes some empirical evidence that may suggest that the perception of conscious control is open to modification (or even manipulation). Wegner observes that one event is inferred to have caused a second event when two requirements are met:
</p>
<ol><li>The first event immediately precedes the second event, and</li>
<li>The first event is consistent with having caused the second event.</li></ol>
<p>For example, if a person hears an explosion and sees a tree fall down that person is likely to infer that the explosion caused the tree to fall over. However, if the explosion occurs after the tree falls down (that is, the first requirement is not met), or rather than an explosion, the person hears the ring of a telephone (that is, the second requirement is not met), then that person is not likely to infer that either noise caused the tree to fall down.
</p><p>Wegner has applied this principle to the inferences people make about their own conscious will. People typically experience a thought that is consistent with a behavior, and then they observe themselves performing this behavior. As a result, people infer that their thoughts must have caused the observed behavior. However, Wegner has been able to manipulate people's thoughts and behaviors so as to conform to or violate the two requirements for causal inference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> Through such work, Wegner has been able to show that people often experience conscious will over behaviors that they have not, in fact, caused – and conversely, that people can be led to experience a lack of will over behaviors they did cause. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Priming_(psychology)" title="Priming (psychology)">priming</a> subjects with information about an effect increases the probability that a person falsely believes is the cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The implication for such work is that the perception of conscious will (which he says might be more accurately labelled as 'the emotion of authorship') is not tethered to the execution of actual behaviors, but is inferred from various cues through an intricate mental process, <i>authorship processing</i>. Although many interpret this work as a blow against the argument for free will, both psychologists<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> and philosophers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Power_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-Power-207">[207]</a></sup> have criticized Wegner's theories.
</p><p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Emily_Pronin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Emily Pronin (page does not exist)">Emily Pronin</a> has argued that the subjective experience of free will is supported by the <a href="/wiki/Introspection_illusion" title="Introspection illusion">introspection illusion</a>. This is the tendency for people to trust the reliability of their own introspections while distrusting the introspections of other people. The theory implies that people will more readily attribute free will to themselves rather than others. This prediction has been confirmed by three of Pronin and Kugler's experiments. When college students were asked about personal decisions in their own and their roommate's lives, they regarded their own choices as less predictable. Staff at a restaurant described their co-workers' lives as more determined (having fewer future possibilities) than their own lives. When weighing up the influence of different factors on behavior, students gave desires and intentions the strongest weight for their own behavior, but rated personality traits as most predictive of other people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup>
</p><p>Caveats have, however, been identified in studying a subject's awareness of mental events, in that the process of introspection itself may alter the experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pockett_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pockett-209">[209]</a></sup>
</p><p>Regardless of the validity of belief in free will, it may be beneficial to understand where the idea comes from. One contribution is randomness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> While it is established that randomness is not the only factor in the perception of the free will, it has been shown that randomness can be mistaken as free will due to its indeterminacy. This misconception applies both when considering oneself and others. Another contribution is choice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> It has been demonstrated that people's belief in free will increases if presented with a simple level of choice. The specificity of the amount of choice is important, as too little or too great a degree of choice may negatively influence belief. It is also likely that the associative relationship between level of choice and perception of free will is influentially bidirectional. It is also possible that one's desire for control, or other basic motivational patterns, act as a third variable.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_experiments">Other experiments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Other experiments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other experiments have also been proposed to test free will. Ender Tosun argues for the reality of free will, based on combined experiments consisting of empirical and thought experiments. In the empirical part of these experiments, experimenter 2 is expected to predict which object experimenter 1 will touch. Experimenter 1 is always able to negate the prediction of experimenter 2. In the thought experiment part, Laplace's demon makes the predictions and experimenter 1 is never able to negate his predictions. Based on the non-correspondence of the predictions of experimenter 2 in the empirical experiment with the predictions of Laplace's demon, and contradictions in the possible layers of causality, Tosun concludes that free will is real. He also extends these experiments to indeterministic processes and real-time brain observations while willing, assuming that an agent has every technological means to probe and rewire his brain. In this thought experiment, experimenter 1 notices the "circuit" of his brain which disables him from willing one of the alternatives, then he probes other circuits to see if he can have the will to rewire that circuit. Experimenter 1 notices that all circuits of his brain being so as to prevent him from rewiring or bypassing the circuits which prevent him from willing to touch one of the objects is impossible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Believing_in_free_will">Believing in free will<span class="anchor" id="Believing_in_free_will"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Believing in free will">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since at least 1959,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nettler1959_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nettler1959-213">[213]</a></sup> free will belief in individuals has been analysed with respect to traits in social behaviour. In general, the concept of free will researched to date in this context has been that of the incompatibilist, or more specifically, the libertarian, that is freedom from determinism.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="What_people_believe">What people believe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: What people believe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Whether people naturally adhere to an incompatibilist model of free will has been questioned in the research. Eddy Nahmias has found that incompatibilism is not intuitive – it was not adhered to, in that determinism does not negate belief in moral responsibility (based on an empirical study of people's responses to moral dilemmas under a deterministic model of reality).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> Edward Cokely has found that incompatibilism is intuitive – it was naturally adhered to, in that determinism does indeed negate belief in moral responsibility in general.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> Joshua Knobe and Shaun Nichols have proposed that incompatibilism may or may not be intuitive, and that it is dependent to some large degree upon the circumstances; whether or not the crime incites an emotional response – for example if it involves harming another human being.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> They found that belief in free will is a cultural universal, and that the majority of participants said that (a) our universe is indeterministic and (b) moral responsibility is not compatible with determinism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies indicate that peoples' belief in free will is inconsistent. Emily Pronin and Matthew Kugler found that people believe they have more free will than others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup>
</p><p>Studies also reveal a correlation between the likelihood of accepting a deterministic model of mind and personality type. For example, Adam Feltz and Edward Cokely found that people of an extrovert personality type are more likely to dissociate belief in determinism from belief in moral responsibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Roy_Baumeister" title="Roy Baumeister">Roy Baumeister</a> and colleagues reviewed literature on the psychological effects of a belief (or disbelief) in free will and found that most people tend to believe in a sort of "naive compatibilistic free will".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAC_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-BAC-220">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup>
</p><p>The researchers also found that people consider acts more "free" when they involve a person opposing external forces, planning, or making random actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Notably, the last behaviour, "random" actions, may not be possible; when participants attempt to perform tasks in a random manner (such as generating random numbers), their behaviour betrays many patterns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Among_philosophers">Among philosophers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Among philosophers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A recent 2020 survey has shown that compatibilism is quite a popular stance among those who specialize in philosophy (59.2%). Belief in libertarianism amounted to 18.8%, while a lack of belief in free will equaled 11.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Among_evolutionary_biologists">Among evolutionary biologists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Among evolutionary biologists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>79 percent of evolutionary biologists said that they believe in free will according to a survey conducted in 2007, only 14 percent chose no free will, and 7 percent did not answer the question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_of_the_belief_itself">Effects of the belief itself</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Effects of the belief itself">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Self-efficacy" title="Self-efficacy">Self-efficacy</a></div>
<p>Baumeister and colleagues found that provoking disbelief in free will seems to cause various negative effects. The authors concluded, in their paper, that it is belief in <a href="/wiki/Determinism" title="Determinism">determinism</a> that causes those negative effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAC_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-BAC-220">[220]</a></sup> Kathleen Vohs has found that those whose belief in free will had been eroded were more likely to cheat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vohs&amp;Sschooler2008_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vohs&amp;Sschooler2008-227">[227]</a></sup> In a study conducted by Roy Baumeister, after participants read an article arguing against free will, they were more likely to lie about their performance on a test where they would be rewarded with cash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baumeister_2009_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-Baumeister_2009-228">[228]</a></sup> Provoking a rejection of free will has also been associated with increased aggression and less helpful behaviour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Baumeister_2009_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-Baumeister_2009-228">[228]</a></sup> However, although these initial studies suggested that believing in free will is associated with more morally praiseworthy behavior, more recent studies (including direct, multi-site replications) with substantially larger sample sizes have reported contradictory findings (typically, no association between belief in free will and moral behavior), casting doubt over the original findings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:40%; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>An alternative explanation builds on the idea that subjects tend to confuse determinism with fatalism... What happens then when agents' self-efficacy is undermined? It is not that their basic desires and drives are defeated. It is rather, I suggest, that they become skeptical that they can control those desires; and in the face of that skepticism, they fail to apply the effort that is needed even to try. If they were tempted to behave badly, then coming to believe in fatalism makes them less likely to resist that temptation.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">—<a href="/wiki/Richard_Holton" title="Richard Holton">Richard Holton</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holton-234">[234]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Moreover, whether or not these experimental findings are a result of actual manipulations in belief in free will is a matter of debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-Holton-234">[234]</a></sup> First of all, free will can at least refer to either <a href="/wiki/Libertarianism_(metaphysics)" title="Libertarianism (metaphysics)">libertarian (indeterministic) free will</a> or <a href="/wiki/Compatibilism" title="Compatibilism">compatibilistic (deterministic) free will</a>. Having participants read articles that simply "disprove free will" is unlikely to increase their understanding of determinism, or the compatibilistic free will that it still permits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_234-2"><a href="#cite_note-Holton-234">[234]</a></sup> In other words, experimental manipulations purporting to "provoke disbelief in free will" may instead cause a belief in <a href="/wiki/Fatalism" title="Fatalism">fatalism</a>, which may provide an alternative explanation for previous experimental findings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_234-3"><a href="#cite_note-Holton-234">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> To test the effects of belief in determinism, it has been argued that future studies would need to provide articles that do not simply "attack free will", but instead focus on explaining determinism and compatibilism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_234-4"><a href="#cite_note-Holton-234">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p><p>Baumeister and colleagues also note that volunteers disbelieving in free will are less capable of <a href="/wiki/Counterfactual_thinking" title="Counterfactual thinking">counterfactual thinking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAC_220-2"><a href="#cite_note-BAC-220">[220]</a></sup> This is worrying because counterfactual thinking ("If I had done something different…") is an important part of learning from one's choices, including those that harmed others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> Again, this cannot be taken to mean that belief in determinism is to blame; these are the results we would expect from increasing people's belief in fatalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_234-5"><a href="#cite_note-Holton-234">[234]</a></sup>
</p><p>Along similar lines, Tyler Stillman has found that belief in free will predicts better job performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_theology">In theology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: In theology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Free_will_in_theology" title="Free will in theology">Free will in theology</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2341" data-file-width="1716" decoding="async" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/170px-Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/255px-Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/340px-Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Rodr%C3%ADguez_-_Saint_Augustine_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Augustine's view of free will and predestination would go on to have a profound impact on Christian theology</div></div></div>
<p>The notions of free will and predestination are heavily debated among Christians. Free will in the Christian sense is the ability to choose between good or evil. Among Catholics, there are those holding to <a href="/wiki/Thomism" title="Thomism">Thomism</a>, adopted from what <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> put forth in the <i><a href="/wiki/Summa_Theologica" title="Summa Theologica">Summa Theologica</a>.</i> There are also some holding to <a href="/wiki/Molinism" title="Molinism">Molinism</a> which was put forth by Jesuit priest <a href="/wiki/Luis_de_Molina" title="Luis de Molina">Luis de Molina</a>. Among Protestants there is <a href="/wiki/Arminianism" title="Arminianism">Arminianism</a>, held primarily by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist_Church" title="Methodist Church">Methodist Churches</a>, and formulated by Dutch theologian <a href="/wiki/Jacobus_Arminius" title="Jacobus Arminius">Jacobus Arminius</a>; and there is also <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> held by most in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed_tradition" title="Reformed tradition">Reformed tradition</a> which was formulated by the French Reformed theologian, <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a>. John Calvin was heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a> views on predestination put forth in his work <i>On the Predestination of the Saints.</i> <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> seems to hold views on predestination similar to Calvinism in his <i><a href="/wiki/On_the_Bondage_of_the_Will" title="On the Bondage of the Will">On the Bondage of the Will</a>,</i> thus rejecting free will. In condemnation of Calvin and Luther views, the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a> declared that "the free will of man, moved and excited by God, can by its consent co-operate with God, Who excites and invites its action; and that it can thereby dispose and prepare itself to obtain the grace of justification. The will can resist grace if it chooses. It is not like a lifeless thing, which remains purely passive. Weakened and diminished by Adam's fall, free will is yet not destroyed in the race (Sess. VI, cap. i and v)." <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a>, the father of the Methodist tradition, taught that humans, enabled by <a href="/wiki/Prevenient_grace" title="Prevenient grace">prevenient grace</a>, have free will through which they can choose God and to do good works, with the goal of <a href="/wiki/Christian_perfection" title="Christian perfection">Christian perfection</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TGC2021_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-TGC2021-239">[239]</a></sup> Upholding <a href="/wiki/Synergism" title="Synergism">synergism</a> (the belief that God and man cooperate in salvation), Methodism teaches that "Our Lord Jesus Christ did so die for all men as to make salvation attainable by every man that cometh into the world. If men are not saved that fault is entirely their own, lying solely in their own unwillingness to obtain the salvation offered to them. (John 1:9; I Thess. 5:9; Titus 2:11-12)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMC1986_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMC1986-240">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Paul the Apostle</a> discusses Predestination in some of his Epistles.
</p><p>"<i>For whom He foreknew, He also predestined to become conformed to the image of His Son, that He might be the first-born among many brethren; and whom He predestined, these He also called; and whom He called, these He also justified; and whom He justified, these He also glorified.</i>" —<a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Romans" title="Epistle to the Romans">Romans</a> 8:29–30
</p><p>"<i>He predestined us to adoption as sons through Jesus Christ to Himself, according to the kind intention of His will.</i>" —<a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Ephesians" title="Epistle to the Ephesians">Ephesians</a> 1:5
</p><p>There are also mentions of moral freedom in what are now termed as 'Deuterocanonical' works which the Orthodox and Catholic Churches use. In Sirach 15 the text states:
</p><p>"Do not say: "It was God's doing that I fell away," for what he hates he does not do. Do not say: "He himself has led me astray," for he has no need of the wicked. Abominable wickedness the Lord hates and he does not let it happen to those who fear him. God in the beginning created human beings and made them subject to their own free choice. If you choose, you can keep the commandments; loyalty is doing the will of God. Set before you are fire and water; to whatever you choose, stretch out your hand. Before everyone are life and death, whichever they choose will be given them. Immense is the wisdom of the Lord; mighty in power, he sees all things. The eyes of God behold his works, and he understands every human deed. He never commands anyone to sin, nor shows leniency toward deceivers."
- Ben Sira‬ ‭15:11-20‬ ‭NABRE
</p><p>The exact meaning of these verses has been debated by Christian theologians throughout history.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">Judaism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Judaism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Free_will_in_theology#Judaism" title="Free will in theology">Free will in theology § Judaism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_(1135-1204).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2389" decoding="async" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_%281135-1204%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_%281135-1204%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_%281135-1204%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_%281135-1204%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_%281135-1204%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_%281135-1204%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_USCapitol_-_Maimonides_(1135-1204).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bas_relief" title="Bas relief">Bas relief</a> of Maimonides in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._House_of_Representatives" title="U.S. House of Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Jewish_thought" title="Jewish thought">Jewish thought</a> the concept of "Free will" (Hebrew: bechirah chofshit בחירה חפשית, bechirah בחירה) is foundational. 
The most succinct statement is by <a href="/wiki/Maimonides" title="Maimonides">Maimonides</a>, in a two part treatment, where human free will is specified as part of the universe's <a href="/wiki/Jewish_principles_of_faith#God_is_the_creator_of_the_universe" title="Jewish principles of faith">Godly design</a>:
</p>
<ol><li>Maimonides's reasoned <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> that human beings must have free will (at least in the context of choosing to do good or evil), as without this, the demands of <a href="/wiki/Nevi%27im#Latter_Prophets" title="Nevi'im">the prophets</a> would have been meaningless, there would be no need for the <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mitzvah" title="Mitzvah"><i>Mitzvot</i></a> ("commandments"), and <a href="/wiki/Jewish_principles_of_faith#Reward_and_punishment" title="Jewish principles of faith">justice could not be administered</a>.</li>
<li>At the same time, Maimonides - and other thinkers - recognizes <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Free_will_in_theology#The_paradox_of_free_will" title="Free will in theology">paradox that will arise</a> given (i) that Judaism simultaneously recognizes God's <a href="/wiki/Omniscience" title="Omniscience">omniscience</a>, and further (ii) the nature of <a href="/wiki/Divine_providence_in_Judaism" title="Divine providence in Judaism">Divine providence as understood in Judaism</a>. (In fact the problem may be seen to overlap <a href="/wiki/Jewish_principles_of_faith#Nature_of_God" title="Jewish principles of faith">several others in Jewish Philosophy</a>.)</li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> the theological issue is not usually how to reconcile free will with God's foreknowledge, but with God's <i>jabr</i>, or divine commanding power. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abu_al-Hasan_al-Ash%27ari" title="Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari">al-Ash'ari</a> developed an "acquisition" or "dual-agency" form of compatibilism, in which human free will and divine <i>jabr</i> were both asserted, and which became a cornerstone of the dominant <a href="/wiki/Ash%27ari" title="Ash'ari">Ash'ari</a> position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia">Shia</a> Islam, Ash'aris understanding of a higher balance toward <a href="/wiki/Predestination" title="Predestination">predestination</a> is challenged by most theologians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> Free will, according to Islamic doctrine is the main factor for man's accountability in his/her actions throughout life. Actions taken by people exercising free will are counted on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Day_of_Judgement" title="Day of Judgement">Day of Judgement</a> because they are their own; however, the free will happens with the permission of God.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The philosopher <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B8ren_Kierkegaard" title="Søren Kierkegaard">Søren Kierkegaard</a> claimed that divine omnipotence cannot be separated from divine goodness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> As a truly omnipotent and good being, God could create beings with true freedom over God. Furthermore, God would voluntarily do so because "the greatest good… which can be done for a being, greater than anything else that one can do for it, is to be truly free."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Plantinga%27s_free-will_defense" title="Alvin Plantinga's free-will defense">Alvin Plantinga's free-will defense</a> is a contemporary expansion of this theme, adding how God, free will, and <a href="/wiki/Problem_of_evil" title="Problem of evil">evil</a> are consistent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some philosophers follow <a href="/wiki/William_of_Ockham" title="William of Ockham">William of Ockham</a> in holding that necessity and possibility are defined with respect to a given point in time and a given matrix of empirical circumstances, and so something that is merely possible from the perspective of one observer may be necessary from the perspective of an omniscient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ockham_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-ockham-250">[250]</a></sup> Some philosophers follow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philo_of_Alexandria" title="Philo of Alexandria">Philo of Alexandria</a>, a philosopher known for his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homocentrism" title="Homocentrism">homocentrism</a>, in holding that free will is a feature of a human's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" title="Soul (spirit)">soul</a>, and thus that non-human <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animals</a> lack free will.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_will&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1093669538">.mw-parser-output .portalbox{padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portalborder{border:solid #aaa 1px}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portalbox.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:175px;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portalborder>ul{padding:0.1em;background:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portalbox>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style><div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint plainlist portalbox portalborder tright" role="navigation">
<ul>
<li><span><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="326" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/18px-Socrates.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/27px-Socrates.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Socrates.png/36px-Socrates.png 2x" width="18"/></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Philosophy" title="Portal:Philosophy">Philosophy portal</a></span></li></ul></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Agency_in_Mormonism" title="Agency in Mormonism">Agency in Mormonism</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Angst#Existentialist_angst" title="Angst">Angst#Existentialist angst</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Argument_from_free_will" title="Argument from free will">Argument from free will</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buridan%27s_ass" title="Buridan's ass">Buridan's ass</a></li>

<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hence the notion of contingency appeared as the very opposition of necessity, so that wherever a thing is considered dependent or relies upon another thing, it is contingent and thus not necessary.</span>

This is not a case where there are several possible candidate solutions and we don't know which is correct. <li id="cite_note-Russell-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Russell_21-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFPaul_Russell2002">Paul Russell (2002). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=cxUfOoGQaPwC&amp;pg=PA14" rel="nofollow">"Chapter 1: Logic, "liberty", and the metaphysics of responsibility"</a>. <i>Freedom and Moral Sentiment: Hume's Way of Naturalizing Responsibility</i>. Oxford University Press. p. 14. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-515290-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-515290-6"><bdi>978-0-19-515290-6</bdi></a>. <q>...the well-known dilemma of determinism. One horn of this dilemma is the argument that if an action was caused or necessitated, then it could not have been done freely, and hence the agent is not responsible for it. The other horn is the argument that if the action was not caused, then it is inexplicable and random, and thus it cannot be attributed to the agent, and hence, again, the agent cannot be responsible for it.... Whether we affirm or deny necessity and determinism, it is impossible to make any coherent sense of moral freedom and responsibility.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Chapter+1%3A+Logic%2C+%22liberty%22%2C+and+the+metaphysics+of+responsibility&amp;rft.btitle=Freedom+and+Moral+Sentiment%3A+Hume%27s+Way+of+Naturalizing+Responsibility&amp;rft.pages=14&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-515290-6&amp;rft.au=Paul+Russell&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DcxUfOoGQaPwC%26pg%3DPA14&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

Oxford University Press. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-162091-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-162091-1"><bdi>978-0-19-162091-1</bdi></a>. <q>Free will, compatibilists argue, is here to stay, and the challenge for science is to figure out exactly how it works and not to peddle silly arguments that deny the undeniable (Dennett 2003)</q></cite><span class="Z3988" <li id="cite_note-Bohr1-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Bohr1_49-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Bohr1_49-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFNiels_Bohr">Niels Bohr. <a class="external text" href="http://www.informationphilosopher.com/solutions/scientists/bohr/fundamental_principles.html" rel="nofollow">"The Atomic Theory and the Fundamental Principles underlying the Description of Nature; <i>Based on a lecture to the Scandinavian Meeting of Natural Scientists and published in Danish in Fysisk Tidsskrift in 1929. Doyle, publisher<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2012-09-14</span></span>. <q>... any observation necessitates an interference with the course of the phenomena, which is of such a nature that it deprives us of the foundation underlying the causal mode of description.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Information+Philosopher%2C+dedicated+to+the+new+information+philosophy&amp;rft.atitle=The+Atomic+Theory+and+the+Fundamental+Principles+underlying+the+Description+of+Nature%3B+Based+on+a+lecture+to+the+Scandinavian+Meeting+of+Natural+Scientists+and+published+in+Danish+in+Fysisk+Tidsskrift+in+1929.+First+published+in+English+in+1934+by+Cambridge+University+Press.&amp;rft.au=Niels+Bohr&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.informationphilosopher.com%2Fsolutions%2Fscientists%2Fbohr%2Ffundamental_principles.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Bohr-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Bohr_50-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Bohr_50-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFNiels_Bohr1933">Niels Bohr (April 1, 1933). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=4RStj6dJDSgC&amp;pg=PA28" rel="nofollow"><i>Light and Life</i></a>. <i>Nature</i>. Vol. 131. pp. 457–459. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1933Natur.131..457B" rel="nofollow">1933Natur.131..457B</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1038%2F131457a0" rel="nofollow">10.1038/131457a0</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-444-89972-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-444-89972-9"><bdi>978-0-444-89972-9</bdi></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:4080545" rel="nofollow">4080545</a>. <q>For instance, it is impossible, from our standpoint, to attach an unambiguous meaning to the view sometimes expressed that the probability of the occurrence of certain atomic processes in the body might be under the direct influence of the will. In fact, according to the generalized interpretation of the psycho-physical parallelism, the freedom of the will must be considered a feature of conscious life that corresponds to functions of the organism that not only evade a causal mechanical description, but resist even a physical analysis carried to the extent required for an unambiguous application of the statistical laws of atomic mechanics. Without entering into metaphysical speculations, I may perhaps add that an analysis of the very concept of explanation would, naturally, begin and end with a renunciation as to explaining our own conscious activity.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Light+and+Life&amp;rft.pages=457-459&amp;rft.date=1933-04-01&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1038%2F131457a0&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A4080545%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F1933Natur.131..457B&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-444-89972-9&amp;rft.au=Niels+Bohr&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D4RStj6dJDSgC%26pg%3DPA28&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span> Full text on line at <a class="external text" href="http://www23.us.archive.org/stream/AtomicPhysicsHumanKnowledge/Bohr-AtomicPhysicsHumanKnowledge_djvu.txt" rel="nofollow">us.archive.org</a>.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-determinism-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-determinism_57-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
The view of <i>scientific determinism</i> goes back to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pierre_Simon_Laplace" title="Pierre Simon Laplace">Laplace</a>: "We ought to regard the present state of the universe as the effect of its antecedent state." For further discussion see <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFJohn_T_Roberts2006">John T Roberts (2006). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=od68ge7aF6wC&amp;pg=PA198" rel="nofollow">"Determinism"</a>.  In Sahotra Sarkar; Jessica Pfeifer; Justin Garson (eds.). <i>The Philosophy of Science: An Encyclopedia. N–Z, Indeks, Volume 1</i>. Psychology Press. pp. 197 <i>ff</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-415-93927-0" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-415-93927-0"><bdi>978-0-415-93927-0</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Determinism&amp;rft.btitle=The+Philosophy+of+Science%3A+An+Encyclopedia.+N%E2%80%93Z%2C+Indeks%2C+Volume+1&amp;rft.pages=197+%27%27ff%27%27&amp;rft.pub=Psychology+Press&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-415-93927-0&amp;rft.au=John+T+Roberts&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dod68ge7aF6wC%26pg%3DPA198&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://philosophy.lander.edu/ethics/notes-determinism.html" rel="nofollow">"Some Varieties of Free Will and Determinism"</a>. <i>Philosophy 302: Ethics</i>. philosophy.lander.edu. 10 September 2009<span class="reference-accessdate">. On this doctrine events throughout eternity have been foreordained by some supernatural power in a causal sequence.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Philosophy+302%3A+Ethics&amp;rft.atitle=Some+Varieties+of+Free+Will+and+Determinism&amp;rft.date=2009-09-10&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fphilosophy.lander.edu%2Fethics%2Fnotes-determinism.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See for example <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFHooft,_G.2001">Hooft, G. (2001). "How does god play dice? (Pre-)determinism at the Planck scale". <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ArXiv_(identifier)" title="ArXiv (identifier)">arXiv</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//arxiv.org/abs/hep-th/0104219" rel="nofollow">hep-th/0104219</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2001hep.th....4219T" rel="nofollow">2001hep.th....4219T</a>. <q>Predeterminism is here defined by the assumption that the experimenter's 'free will' in deciding what to measure (such as his choice to measure the x- or the y-component of an electron's spin), is in fact limited by deterministic laws, hence not free at all</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=How+does+god+play+dice%3F+%28Pre-%29determinism+at+the+Planck+scale&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft_id=info%3Aarxiv%2Fhep-th%2F0104219&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2001hep.th....4219T&amp;rft.au=Hooft%2C+G.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span> <span class="cs1-hidden-error citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Cite_journal" title="Template:Cite journal">cite journal</a>}}</code>: </span><span class="cs1-hidden-error citation-comment">Cite journal requires <code class="cs1-code">|journal=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#missing_periodical" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span>, and <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSukumar,_CV1996">Sukumar, CV (1996). "A new paradigm for science and architecture". <i>City</i>. <b>1</b> (1–2): 181–83. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1080%2F13604819608900044" rel="nofollow">10.1080/13604819608900044</a>. <q>Quantum Theory provided a beautiful description of the behaviour of isolated atoms and nuclei and small aggregates of elementary particles. Modern science recognized that predisposition rather than predeterminism is what is widely prevalent in nature.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=City&amp;rft.atitle=A+new+paradigm+for+science+and+architecture&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.issue=1%E2%80%932&amp;rft.pages=181-83&amp;rft.date=1996&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1080%2F13604819608900044&amp;rft.au=Sukumar%2C+CV&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFBorst,_C.1992">Borst, C. (1992). "Leibniz and the compatibilist account of free will". <i>Studia Leibnitiana</i>. <b>24</b> (1): 49–58. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JSTOR_(identifier)" title="JSTOR (identifier)">JSTOR</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.jstor.org/stable/40694201" rel="nofollow">40694201</a>. <q>Leibniz presents a clear case of a philosopher who does not think that predeterminism requires universal causal determinism</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Studia+Leibnitiana&amp;rft.atitle=Leibniz+and+the+compatibilist+account+of+free+will&amp;rft.volume=24&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=49-58&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.jstor.org%2Fstable%2F40694201%23id-name%3DJSTOR&amp;rft.au=Borst%2C+C.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Society1971-98"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Society1971_98-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFar_Western_Philosophy_of_Education_Society1971">Far Western Philosophy of Education Society (1971). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=spkpAQAAMAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>Proceedings of the Annual Meeting of the Far Western Philosophy of Education Society</i></a>. Far Western Philosophy of Education Society. p. 12<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">20 December</span> 2012</span>. <q>"Determinism" is, in essence, the position holding that all behavior is caused by prior behavior. "Predeterminism" is the position holding that all behavior is caused by conditions predating behavior altogether (such impersonal boundaries as "the human conditions", instincts, the will of God, inherent knowledge, fate, and such).</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proceedings+of+the+Annual+Meeting+of+the+Far+Western+Philosophy+of+Education+Society&amp;rft.pages=12&amp;rft.pub=Far+Western+Philosophy+of+Education+Society.&amp;rft.date=1971&amp;rft.au=Far+Western+Philosophy+of+Education+Society&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DspkpAQAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/predeterminism" rel="nofollow">"Predeterminism"</a>. <i>Merriam-Webster Dictionary</i>. Merriam-Webster, Incorporated<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">20 December</span> 2012</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Predeterminism&amp;rft.btitle=Merriam-Webster+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=Merriam-Webster%2C+Incorporated&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.merriam-webster.com%2Fdictionary%2Fpredeterminism&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span> See for example <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFOrmond,_A.T.1894">Ormond, A.T. (1894). <a class="external text" href="https://zenodo.org/record/1429090" rel="nofollow">"Freedom and psycho-genesis"</a>. <i>Psychological Review</i>. <b>1</b> (3): 217–29. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1037%2Fh0065249" rel="nofollow">10.1037/h0065249</a>. <q>The problem of predeterminism is one that involves the factors of heredity and environment, and the point to be debated here is the relation of the present self that chooses to these predetermining agencies</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Psychological+Review&amp;rft.atitle=Freedom+and+psycho-genesis&amp;rft.volume=1&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=217-29&amp;rft.date=1894&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1037%2Fh0065249&amp;rft.au=Ormond%2C+A.T.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fzenodo.org%2Frecord%2F1429090&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span>, and <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFGarris,_M.D.1992">Garris, M.D.;  et al. (1992). "A Platform for Evolving Genetic Automata for Text Segmentation (GNATS)". <i>Science of Artificial Neural Networks</i>. <b>1710</b>: 714–24. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/1992SPIE.1710..714G" rel="nofollow">1992SPIE.1710..714G</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1117%2F12.140132" rel="nofollow">10.1117/12.140132</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:62639035" rel="nofollow">62639035</a>. <q>However, predeterminism is not completely avoided. If the codes within the genotype are not designed properly, then the organisms being evolved will be fundamentally handicapped.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Science+of+Artificial+Neural+Networks&amp;rft.atitle=A+Platform+for+Evolving+Genetic+Automata+for+Text+Segmentation+%28GNATS%29&amp;rft.volume=1710&amp;rft.pages=714-24&amp;rft.date=1992&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A62639035%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1117%2F12.140132&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F1992SPIE.1710..714G&amp;rft.au=Garris%2C+M.D.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-100">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSherman,_H.1981">Sherman, H. (1981). "Marx and determinism". <i>Journal of Economic Issues</i>. <b>15</b> (1): 61–71. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1080%2F00213624.1981.11503814" rel="nofollow">10.1080/00213624.1981.11503814</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JSTOR_(identifier)" title="JSTOR (identifier)">JSTOR</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.jstor.org/stable/4224996" rel="nofollow">4224996</a>. <q>Many religions of the world have considered that the path of history is predetermined by God or Fate. <li id="cite_note-naturalism-127"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-naturalism_127-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A key exponent of this view was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willard_van_Orman_Quine" title="Willard van Orman Quine">Willard van Orman Quine</a>. See <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFHylton,_Peter2010">Hylton, Peter (Apr 30, 2010). <a class="external text" href="http://plato.stanford.edu/archives/fall2010/entries/quine/" rel="nofollow">"Willard van Orman Quine"</a>. Zalta (ed.). <i>The Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy (Fall 2010 Edition)</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Willard+van+Orman+Quine&amp;rft.btitle=The+Stanford+Encyclopedia+of+Philosophy+%28Fall+2010+Edition%29&amp;rft.date=2010-04-30&amp;rft.au=Hylton%2C+Peter&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fplato.stanford.edu%2Farchives%2Ffall2010%2Fentries%2Fquine%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>

A thoughtful list of careful distinctions regarding the application of empirical science to these issues is found in <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFStoljar,_Daniel2009">Stoljar, Daniel (Sep 9, 2009). <a class="external text" href="http://plato.stanford.edu/archives/fall2009/entries/physicalism/#12" rel="nofollow">"Physicalism: §12 – Physicalism and the physicalist world picture"</a>. <li id="cite_note-148"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-148">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Kant argued that, in order that human life is not just a "dream" (a random or projected by subjects juxtaposition of moments), the temporality of event A as before or after B must submit to a rule. An established order then implies the existence of some necessary conditions and causes, that is: sufficient bases (a so-called sufficient reason is the coincidence of all the necessary conditions). Without established causality, both <a href="/wiki/Transcendental_apperception" title="Transcendental apperception">in subject</a> and in the external world, the passing of time would be impossible, because it is essentially directional. See <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Critique_of_Pure_Reason/Volume_1/Division_1#B._Second_Analogy._Principle_of_the_Succession_of_Time_According_to_the_Law_of_Causality._All_changes_take_place_according_to_the_law_of_the_connection_of_Cause_and_Effect." title="s:Critique of Pure Reason/Volume 1/Division 1">online text of his proof</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-149">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Schopenhauer, who by the way continued and simplified Kant's system, argued (among others basing on optical illusions and the "initial processing") that it is the intellect or even the brain what generates the image of the world out of something else, by <i>concluding from effects, e.g. optical, about appropriate causes</i>, e.g. concrete physical objects. Intellect in his works is strictly connected with recognizing causes and effects and associating them, it is somewhat close to the contemporary view of <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_cortex" title="Cerebral cortex">cerebral cortex</a> and formation of associations. The intellectuality of all perception implied then of course that causality is rooted in the world, precedes and enables experience. See <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Page:On_the_Fourfold_Root,_and_On_the_Will_in_Nature.djvu/90" title="s:Page:On the Fourfold Root, and On the Will in Nature.djvu/90">online text of his proof</a></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Freeman-152"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Freeman_152-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFreeman,_Walter_J.2009">Freeman, Walter J. (2009). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=G5CaTnNksgkC&amp;pg=PA88" rel="nofollow">"Consciousness, intentionality and causality"</a>.  In Susan Pockett; WP Banks; Shaun Gallagher (eds.). <i>Does Consciousness Cause Behavior?</i>. MIT Press. p. 88. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-262-51257-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-262-51257-2"><bdi>978-0-262-51257-2</bdi></a>. <q>Circular causality departs so strongly from the classical tenets of necessity, invariance, and precise temporal order that the only reason to call it that is to satisfy the human habitual need for causes.... The very strong appeal of agency to explain events may come from the subjective experience of cause and effect that develops early in human life, before the acquisition of language...the question I raise here is whether brains share this property with other material objects in the world.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Consciousness%2C+intentionality+and+causality&amp;rft.btitle=Does+Consciousness+Cause+Behavior%3F&amp;rft.pages=88&amp;rft.pub=MIT+Press&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-262-51257-2&amp;rft.au=Freeman%2C+Walter+J.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DG5CaTnNksgkC%26pg%3DPA88&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-Stump-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Stump_155-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">

A discussion of the roles of will, intellect and passions in Aquinas' teachings is found in <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFStump,_Eleonore2003">Stump, Eleonore (2003). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=1GvL3eKhoM8C&amp;pg=PA278" rel="nofollow">"Intellect and will"</a>. <i>Aquinas, </i>Arguments of the philosophers series<i><span></span></i>. Routledge (Psychology Press). pp. 278 <i>ff</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-415-02960-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-415-02960-5"><bdi>978-0-415-02960-5</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Intellect+and+will&amp;rft.btitle=Aquinas%2C+Arguments+of+the+philosophers+series&amp;rft.pages=278+%27%27ff%27%27&amp;rft.pub=Routledge+%28Psychology+Press%29&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-415-02960-5&amp;rft.au=Stump%2C+Eleonore&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D1GvL3eKhoM8C%26pg%3DPA278&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-OConnor0-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-OConnor0_156-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFTimothy_O'Connor2010">Timothy O'Connor (Oct 29, 2010). <a class="external text" href="http://plato.stanford.edu/archives/sum2011/entries/freewill/" rel="nofollow">"Free Will"</a>.  In Edward N. Zalta (ed.). <i>The Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy (Summer 2011 Edition)</i>. The Metaphysics Research Lab Center for the Study of Language and Information, Stanford University. <q>Philosophers who distinguish <i>freedom of action</i> and <i>freedom of will</i> do so because our success in carrying out our ends depends in part on factors wholly beyond our control. Furthermore, there are always external constraints on the range of options we can meaningfully try to undertake. As the presence or absence of these conditions and constraints are not (usually) our responsibility, it is plausible that the central loci of our responsibility are our choices, or "willings".</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Free+Will&amp;rft.btitle=The+Stanford+Encyclopedia+of+Philosophy+%28Summer+2011+Edition%29&amp;rft.pub=The+Metaphysics+Research+Lab+Center+for+the+Study+of+Language+and+Information%2C+Stanford+University&amp;rft.date=2010-10-29&amp;rft.au=Timothy+O%27Connor&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fplato.stanford.edu%2Farchives%2Fsum2011%2Fentries%2Ffreewill%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.newadvent.org/cathen/01656a.htm" rel="nofollow">"Catholic Encyclopedia: Appetite"</a>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2012-08-13</span></span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Catholic+Encyclopedia%3A+Appetite&amp;rft.pub=Newadvent.org&amp;rft.date=1907&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.newadvent.org%2Fcathen%2F01656a.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-158"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-158">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.newadvent.org/summa/1083.htm" rel="nofollow">"Summa Theologica: Free-will (Prima Pars, Q. 83)"</a>. Newadvent.org<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2012-08-13</span></span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Summa+Theologica%3A+Free-will+%28Prima+Pars%2C+Q.+83%29&amp;rft.pub=Newadvent.org&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.newadvent.org%2Fsumma%2F1083.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-159"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-159">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Thomas Aquinas, <i>Summa Theologiae</i>, Q83 A1.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-160"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-160">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Further discussion of this compatibilistic theory can be found in Thomas' <i>Summa contra gentiles</i>, Book III about Providence, c. 88–91 (260–267), where it is postulated that everything has its cause and it is again and again in detail referred also to all individual choices of man etc., even refuting opposite views. <a class="external text" href="http://dhspriory.org/thomas/ContraGentiles3b.htm#88" rel="nofollow">Here the online text of the Summa</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20171123185058/http://dhspriory.org/thomas/ContraGentiles3b.htm#88" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 2017-11-23 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. In order to avoid, at least in concept, the absolution of man of any guilt he then notes the contingency of all that takes place, i.e. lack of <i>direct</i> necessity from God strictly with regard to a concrete ("contingent") act. A typical choice was not separately ordained to be so-and-so by God; St. Thomas says the choice is not necessary, but in fact that apparently means it was <i>contingent</i> with regard to God and the law of nature (as a specific case that could have not existed in other circumstances), and <i>necessary</i> with regard to its direct previous cause in will and intellect. (The contingency, or fortuity, is even intuitive under modern <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">chaos theory</a>, where one can try to show that more and more developed products appearing in the evolution of a universe or, simpler, an automaton are <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">chaotic</a> with regard to its principles.)</span>
</li>

Oxford University Press. p. 5. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-973339-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-973339-2"><bdi>978-0-19-973339-2</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=I.+The+free+will+problem+%E2%80%93+real+or+illusory&amp;rft.btitle=The+Philosophy+of+Free+Will%3A+Essential+Readings+from+the+Contemporary+Debates&amp;rft.pages=5&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-973339-2&amp;rft.au=Paul+Russell&amp;rft.au=Oisin+Deery&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DCLyi7nmzr28C%26pg%3DPA5&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Gier-162"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Gier_162-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Gier_162-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Gier_162-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Gier, Nicholas and Kjellberg, Paul. <li id="cite_note-163"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-163">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFFlood2004">Flood, Gavin (2004). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=fapXqp-JSL0C&amp;q=kaivalya" rel="nofollow"><i>The ascetic self: subjectivity, memory and tradition</i></a>. Cambridge University Press. p. 73. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-521-60401-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-521-60401-7"><bdi>978-0-521-60401-7</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+ascetic+self%3A+subjectivity%2C+memory+and+tradition&amp;rft.pages=73&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-521-60401-7&amp;rft.aulast=Flood&amp;rft.aufirst=Gavin&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfapXqp-JSL0C%26q%3Dkaivalya&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-235"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-235">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFMiles2011">Miles, J.B. <li id="cite_note-236"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-236">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some studies have been conducted indicating that people react strongly to the way in which mental determinism is described, when reconciling it with moral responsibility. Eddy Nahmias has noted that when people's actions are framed with respect to their beliefs and desires (rather than their neurological underpinnings), they are more likely to dissociate determinism from moral responsibility. See <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFNahmiasD._Justin_CoatesTrevor_Kvaran2007">Nahmias, Eddy; D. Justin Coates; Trevor Kvaran (2007-09-01). "Free Will, Moral Responsibility, and Mechanism: Experiments on Folk Intuitions". <i>Midwest Studies in Philosophy</i>. <b>31</b> (1): 214–42. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1111%2Fj.1475-4975.2007.00158.x" rel="nofollow">10.1111/j.1475-4975.2007.00158.x</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISSN_(identifier)" title="ISSN (identifier)">ISSN</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/1475-4975" rel="nofollow">1475-4975</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:15648622" rel="nofollow">15648622</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Midwest+Studies+in+Philosophy&amp;rft.atitle=Free+Will%2C+Moral+Responsibility%2C+and+Mechanism%3A+Experiments+on+Folk+Intuitions&amp;rft.volume=31&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=214-42&amp;rft.date=2007-09-01&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.semanticscholar.org%2FCorpusID%3A15648622%23id-name%3DS2CID&amp;rft.issn=1475-4975&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1111%2Fj.1475-4975.2007.00158.x&amp;rft.aulast=Nahmias&amp;rft.aufirst=Eddy&amp;rft.au=D.+Justin+Coates&amp;rft.au=Trevor+Kvaran&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFree+will"></span></span>
</li>
